\clearpage
\section{Summary of Results}
\paragraph{}
For brevity, we only list the RBO scores of the networks instead of explicitly stating "The rank-biased overlap between a network and itself is $"$.1" or 1.0"$ where appropriate (``" marks are mentioned since RBO is typically given as a value from 0 to 1, with 1 indicating a perfect ranking).
\paragraph{}
Note that CBOWIT is initialized with the 100-dimensional embeddings that took the longest time among all models to train as the preliminary embedding vectors. After projecting onto a 3-dimensional space and visualizing, it was found that CBOWIT network was the most clustered and condensed. Despite that which would not suggest superior similarity with the Spanish part of Wortschatz corpora, it turned out that the CBOWIT network actually outperformed all the others that do perform well in visualization (we will come back to this soon). Another noteworthy observation was the model performing best on normalized miw word2vec embeddings, which makes sense since the structured database and the information retrieval algorithm were all based on normalized miw representations.

\section{Visualization in Decision Trees}
\paragraph{}
Given that our main comparison is on similarity vectors, the following steps regard to illustrating the directions encoded by models: 1. Project the original embedding from regular\ computed Semantic boundary of limited number of readjusted Spanish words from applying Douget and Timmers's Ratheon linear transformation, equipped with suggested dimensions obtained by numopt of the cosine similarity maps, as sparse vectors spanned by all their eigenvectors. Illustrate a node in 2D space, and directly apply scatter plot as the plot function. 2. Upon attaining 3D structure projections, and borrow similar technique in that of the SC codes, since it too, is quite perceivably detected in some cross-analysis of the balanced clustering parameter with average Difference-Of-Avg similarities. Concretely, we can retrieve the first four dimensions from each model, 3 specifying (x, y, z) and 1 explaining color intensity maps, and put them into t-SNE or PCA to re-project to a 2D orthogonal plane to observe whether a linear subspace can be formulated. Using the re-shuffled 2D outputs, facilitate K-means clustering and evaluate the consistentcy of reproducing assigning labels.

\section{Graphical Illustration in Gephi}
\paragraph{}
According to the specification assignments, we are required to show the main procedures of network visualization: 1. Could large connected nodes at the center, and initialize input some of them, say for 5000 (10\%) and limit link distances to edge connection points by evenly spaced parameterized weight on the possibilities of word proximity 2. Plotting, through a simple network diagram, which figures all the vertices in illustration format in order to explore the links between different label types for our test cases. 3. Used edge-based visualization techniques to explore label implications and dependence the neural networks of various parameters we have examined, e.g. ratios of positive feedback to negative feedbacks, activation values in the function of embedding dimensions etc.. 4. Save the network to a binary file as a matrix would usually do. Look at the difference among all kernel descriptors and start a manifold learning with Graph2Vec and hope to get a new least-dimensional sub-space. Additionally, 5. We can then write an implementation located in the correct folder of make an example code of adjacency matrices, same as the one previously shown, with graphical guidelines and instructions to split a co-occur network into n subnets of equal size (number of nodes and links). Analyze and submit your report based on the obtained scores in regards to cooperativeness and embeddedness, etc. according to QAP test.

\section{Organize}
From the above metrics and representations, we will have to demonstrate how the fitting performances change over different ratios, token threshold and singularization/pluralization.

\chapter{Conclusion}
\paragraph{}
To summarize, the research outcomes of this project include: 1. Both word2vec and Poincare models are negligibly effective given original corpora; 2. when the first probed vector control comes, in most cases, no further improvement is identifiable, 3. In terms of similarity computation, words stemming from Wortschatz project share similar syntax and parts-of-speech, and semantic forming based on categorized knowledge graphs though in a smaller scale output.
